< review>
I've had issues in the past with deliveries a few years back, but I actually found out that google maps has my address with a picture and location pointed at the wrong house (my neighbor's house). I didn't find out until quite recently.

I've sent emails in the past about misdelivered packages (with tracking numbers) a long time ago and they actually did better! I left a note on my mailbox about leaving packages right at my door because I've had a package stolen by a passerby even though I was home all day. It was frustrating back then. The usps people who deliver to my place no longer misdeliver my packages or leave them in the open for theft. They knock before leaving a package, which I greatly appreciate.

The delivery people are nice enough and the post office people have not been rude when I make a mistake or want to deliver/pick up something.

If they get temps around the holidays, I wouldn't be surprised with misdeliveries since they are not acquainted with my address.

Anyway, I'm really happy with their service and have been for quite a while now. They are very responsive through email. Calling hasn't been the best experiences, but not the worst, and as long as you are nice they will work with you. I'm sure they work really hard and have been through a lot.< /review>

<time>1606006730198</time><rating>5<//rating>< text>
Totally great place to spend a morning or afternoon, or the whole day.

Plants, trees, and flowers that you won't see often unless you do a lot of world wide traveling.

My wife and I spent the afternoon stopping and gawking at the wonderful plants.  We were here on the 21st of November and the fall colors were also glorious.

A fun place to use an app to help identify flowers and leaves.

The only drawback was the lack of bathroom facilities and drinking water.</text>

<Name>Kimberly Hicks</Name>< Time>
1611443212306<//Time>
<Rate>5< /Rate>< text>
Nice design. Started at the western end and saw so many varieties of oaks. We had no idea there were so many, and we still would not if they hadn't taken the time to mark them; and not with little metal stakes or tags. No, the markers in this part of the arboretum were talented art installations of ceramic on concrete.
Then we went on around the pond. All the other plants are marked, though not with the same flare.
Altogether we walked 2.5 miles, but we could have walked further.
At the eastern end of the pond is a "creek." At that point there is a bridge that we didn't cross, and there are more as the path meanders along the water.
The bridges are located frequently enough that if one begins to regret not crossing over at the last one to begin the return to their car, there will be another coming along soon thereafter.
It made a beautiful after lunch walk.< /text>

<userid>106274033533152591659< /userid><name>David Dao< /name><Time>1613269753213</Time><Rating>5< /Rating>< Review>
First time in this store.  I was disappointed with the succulent display inside the store until I realize they have a lot more in the back garden. I love the variety of different types of succulents and some of them I have not seen at other local stores.  There prices are very reasonable.  They range from $4 up to $16 based on their sizes.  Personally, I like to get the small ones so I can grow them myself.  I picked up 9 for a total of $40.

The staff at the store are very friendly and helpful.  They checked in with us regularly to see if we need help but they also allow us enough privacy to look around on our own.  One of the succulents I asked for was out of stock, the lady offered to take down my number and call when she has it. This kind of personal service is hard to find nowadays.   I used to go to the one on Bayshore for my succulents and other plants.  This will be my go to place for succulents from now on.< /Review>

<text>This place is so cute! Perfect for a fun and interactive date. You can build your own terrariums or plant plants in all sorts of containers. You can bring your own container and/or plant if you want and just pay to plant it at the plant bar. They provide soil and rocks and decor for your planter as well included with the planter bar fee ($10 for a 4‚Äù container, add $2 per inch I think is the pricing).

They also have classes for more advanced vertical planters as well as basic classes. You can go in and just buy plants if you want. There‚Äôs a big selection. They also sell salt lamps, soaps, water bottles, socks, and other knick knacks.

Some of their customizable options for creating decor for your home are really cool.< /text><pics>None<//pics><Resp>None<//Resp><gmapID>0x808f7e5959ad85a7:0x63c4d87dbc4c93bb< /gmapID></record>

< review>
The store itself--awesome.  Great selection of succulents and succulent accessories, including terrariums, hanging pots, and even tiny succulent necklaces.  Prices seem to be slightly cheaper than at Flora Grubb.  Succulence gets only 3 stars, though, because the service was pretty poor.  I was in the back room putting together a sort of potting kit for my housemate, and while the associate would say things like "let me know if you need any help," when I'd ask questions, he'd give me short answers as if I was asking stupid questions.  I had already told him that I wasn't very knowledgeable about this stuff, so no need to treat me like I'm stupid.  Overall I felt really uncomfortable around him.  The woman at the cash register, who seemed to be a manager, was much nicer and more helpful; just wish she was the one in the back helping customers out.</review>
